School Social Work in Iowa: Past, Present and Future

Author: Clark, James P11 School Social Work Services, Iowa Dept Public Instruction

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61464995?accountid=14667

Abstract: The history of school social work in IA is traced, & a report on the current status of schools social work in the state is provided as background for identifying key future trends & issues. The development of school social work certification standards & the related implications for social work education, the need to develop an empirical base for practice, the need to recognize & respond to the shifting emphases & changing needs of special education, the challenge of promoting school social work within the school & in the community, & the need for involvement in professional organizations, are trends & issues discussed relative to the future of school social work. 8 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Impact of Legal Mandates on School Social Services: Implications for School Social Work in Special Education

Author: Templeman, Peter R11 Franklin Center/Central School, Dubuque, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61511279?accountid=14667

Abstract: The focus of this article traces the impact of specific court decisions on the rights of handicapped students. The cumulative effect of several court actions over time is discussed, which tends to develop a picture of broadening support for students requiring special education services. Questions are raised relating to the effect of the court decisions & later laws on the delivery of services to handicapped children. Additional points of view are developed suggesting the changes occurring to the models of school social work practice. The participation of school social workers in the process of policy development is also outlined. Adapted from the source document.

Social Work and the Mentally Retarded Child

Author: Monfils, Michael J11 Nebraska Psychiatric Instit, Omaha

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61439992?accountid=14667

Abstract: Increasing numbers of mentally retarded children are being served in the public schools rather than in institutional settings. These children are an underserved population posing significant challenges to educators & school social workers. This paper examines & describes three critical roles in school social work practice with retarded children: (1) intervention with parents & family; (2) consultation & education with key school personnel; & (3) community development & education. The author believes that school social workers can provide valuable leadership in meeting the developmental needs of the retarded child & his or her family. 20 References. Adapted from the source document.

A Flexible Contingency Program as a Classroom Management Alternative

Author: Singer, Marc A1; Martin, Judith A1 Lakeland Area Education Agency, Algona, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61511316?accountid=14667

Abstract: The present study combined peer sampling & direct observational techniques with a flexible contingency intervention design to reduce the inappropriate behavior of a first grade student. A behavioral aide recorded the frequency of target behavior during identification, baseline, & intervention phases. Significant behavioral improvement along with positive growth in the student's self-concept & peer skills were results of intervention. Elementary school-aged children spend approximately a quarter of the day in the school setting. The educational & social experiences they encounter in school have a significant influence on learning, social relationships, & self-concept. If school experiences are not of a positive nature, a child's self-concept & achievement may fall below that of others in the class. The degree of difference could lead to conflicts &/or disruptive behavior in the classroom. 3 Figures, 12 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+School+Social+Work&amp;rft.atitle=A+Flexible+Contingency+Program+as+a+Classroom+Management+Alternative&amp;rft.au=Singer%2C+Marc+A%3BMartin%2C+Judith+A&amp;rft.aulast=Singer&amp;rft.aufirst=Marc&amp;rft.date=1986-04-01&amp;rft.volume=1&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=45&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Journal+of+School+Social+Work&amp;rft.issn=&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Collecting Health/Developmental Data: Guidelines for Practice in Educational Assessment

Author: Palumbo, Ron1; Wiarda, Sally Petefish1 c/o Wiarda -- Area Education Agency 6, Marshalltown, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61531902?accountid=14667

Abstract: This essay addresses the problems commonly encountered in collecting health/developmental data as part of a diagnostic educational assessment. It proposes that the search for solutions needs to begin with clarifying the purposes for gathering this data. Suggestions are made for general criteria in selecting the evaluator; major components to be included; & guidelines or interpreting & reporting data collected. These recommendations for practice are based upon the authors' combined experience in the field. 10 References. Adapted from the source document.

Home-Based Family Intervention in Special Education Programs

Author: Kopper-Roland, Beverly A11 AEA 6, Marshalltown, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61468973?accountid=14667

Abstract: A home-based intervention program was designed for noncompliance in which parents were the change agents for their 7-year-old mentally disabled son. Prior to reviewing & implementing the behavioral intervention techniques used, significant family stress factors were addressed. Modeling, demonstration, coaching, & concrete examples were used extensively in view of the parents' estimated borderline intelligence. Results showed the treatment plan reduced the number of reminders necessary for the child to clean his room to a range specified as acceptable by the parents. This improvement coincided with teacher reports indicating an increase in the student's on-task behavior, keeping his desk clean, & self-confidence. 1 Figure, 40 References. Adapted from the source document.

Diagnostic Reports and Educational Relevance

Author: Forster, Irving11 Keystone AEA, Decorah, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61494955?accountid=14667

Abstract: Educational relevance of diagnostic reports should be determined by the major function of the school, ie, structured learning. Three categories of information appear to be universally relevant: energy, motivation, & style. Information in these areas tends to have immediate relevance to teachers, who have the primary responsibility for structured learning. Two case examples illustrate the use of these 3 concepts. 12 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Home-School Coordinator: One School District's Attempt to Reach Out to Families in Need

Author: Phillips, Karen11 Grinnell-Newburg Schools

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61419092?accountid=14667

Abstract: The Grinnell-Newburg School Board responded positively to a proposal written by elementary teachers to hire a Home-School Coordinator to serve the three elementary schools in the district. The program's emphasis is on 25 families in the district who are experiencing stress & who are not already receiving services from another agency. The Home-School Coordinator position provides a blending of traditional school counselor & school social worker roles. Adapted from the source document.

Encopresis: It Can Be Cured

Author: Knepper, Lorraine1; Sturdevant, Ray1 c/o Sturdevant -- Specialized Children's Clinic, Sioux City, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61468924?accountid=14667

Abstract: Until recently, there had been little improvement in the treatment of encopretic children, despite all the sophisticated psychiatric therapies that could be marshaled for them. The U of Iowa Medical Center in Iowa City has adapted a medical treatment that has proved successful for most of the children, provided the procedure is followed faithfully by the parents. The relief of being free of soiling is understandably wonderful to the children & those who know & work with them. 1 Reference. Adapted from the source document.

Survey of Iowa School Social Workers

Author: Flieder, Al1; Henderson, Heather1 School Social Work Program, Grant Wood AEA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469478?accountid=14667

Abstract: During spring 1986, a survey of IA's school social workers was accomplished. It obtained practitioner responses in six areas pertaining to involvement & improvement of the Iowa School Social Work Assoc (ISSWA), membership in other professional organizations, & private practice activities. Additionally, it yielded a rank-ordered list of priorities for action that ISSWA would receive support pursuing. This article presents major findings from the survey, reports activities that have already been initiated by ISSWA leadership, & suggests implications for further action. 2 Tables, 1 Appendix. Adapted from the source document.

Mutual Storytelling

Author: Kehrwald, Donald J11 AEA 12

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469493?accountid=14667

Abstract: I was first introduced to the Mutual Storytelling Technique in fall 1984 at a conference presented by Dr. Richard A. Gardner titled "Therapeutic Techniques with Children." For the past three years, I have been developing my own skills with mutual storytelling. I have discovered that it is a valuable tool in my repertoire of therapy skills with elementary-age children. In this article, I outline the steps in the Mutual Storytelling Technique & include observations from my own experiences. 1 Reference. Adapted from the source document.

School Social Work in Iowa: Opportunities for the Future

Author: Clark, James P11 School Social Work Services, Iowa Dept Education

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61470671?accountid=14667

Abstract: The potential for future growth & development of school social work programs & services in IA is discussed in relation to two major special education initiatives, ie, implementation of services to infants & toddlers under Part H of the 1986 Education of the Handicapped Amendments (P. L. 99-457), & a comprehensive effort to renew IA's special education service delivery system. New state school standards dealing with services to students at risk & re-authorization of the Education Consolidation & Improvement Act are also discussed in relation to future opportunities for school social work program development & expansion. 3 References. Adapted from the source document.

Author: Kehrwald, Donald J1; Lewis, Gary E1 AEA 12, Sioux City, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469511?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article describes the development & implementation of building-level Child Study Teams. The Special Needs Program as a Social Skill Building Tool

Author: Singer, Marc A11 Lakeland Area Education Agency

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61511350?accountid=14667

Abstract: This study summarizes first-year results from the Special Needs Program. Based on a behavior deficit, learning model approach, this service was developed to build & enhance the social skills in targeted students grades kindergarten through eight. Results showed some positive growth in targeted social skills. The implications of this learning format for future social skills training are discussed. 2 Appendixes, 13 References. Author: Grooters, Lyn1; Weber, Ellen1 Des Moines Public Schools, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469004?accountid=14667

Abstract: The Des Moines Public Schools with the assistance of social workers have developed a Crisis Response Plan to be activated when any type of death, serious injury, or disaster occurs that affects students & faculty. Author: Alexander, M Paul11 Lower Kuskokwim School District, Bethel, AK

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61465020?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article discusses the role of the school social worker in helping parents deal with anger towards their children. Included are suggestions for anger education, parent counseling parent skills training, & other ways of coping with parental anger. In particular, parents need to develop "anger skills" in order to model appropriate expression of anger for their children. Adapted from the source document.

Attention-Deficity Hyperactivity Disorder: Issues in Definition and Diagnosis

Author: Reitz, Cindy1; Lindgren, Nancy1 Northern Trails Area Education Agency 2, Clear Lake, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469715?accountid=14667

Abstract: Literature contains extensive research information on the diagnosis & treatment of attention-deficit hyperactivity disorder (ADHD). Children with ADHD are seen in a multitude of settings including those served by school social workers. To do competent assessment, treatment, planning, referral, advocacy, & therapy with ADHD children & their families, knowledge of its many facets & treatments is essential. This article presents a comprehensive review of historical & current research findings, etiologies, & assessment procedures for use by the school social worker who serves ADHD children & their families. A future article will review treatment issues. 36 References. Adapted from the source document.

Attention-Deficity Hyperactivity Disorder: An Annotated Bibliography (Part I)

Author: Verrette, Sallie C11 Heartland Area Education Agency, Newton, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469018?accountid=14667

Abstract: This bibliography is part of a project intended to provide school social workers with readily accessible information on a variety of specialized topics. The topic of this bibliography is research on attention-deficit hyperactivity disorder published since 1980. From approximately one hundred articles, thirty-one were selected for inclusion & briefly summarized. Topics include medication, non-drug therapy, characteristics & etiology of attention-deficit hyperactivity disorder, & longitudinal & prospective studies. Part I presents articles in the category of characteristics & etiology & medication. The other topics will be included in Part II, which will appear in the next issue. Adapted from the source document.

Perceptions of Behavioral Adjustments as Predictors of Academic Achievement

Author: Nunn, Gerald D1; Montgomery, John D1 Area Education Agency 6, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61511390?accountid=14667

Abstract: The present study examined students' perceptions of behavioral adjustment to home, school, & peers as predictive of subsequent academic achievement with 268 children (131 males & 137 females) in grades five through eight. Statistically significant relationships supported the relationship between these factors in understanding psychosocial aspects of achievement. Implications of these findings are discussed. 1 Table, 8 References. Adapted from the source document.

Author: Clark, James P11 Bureau Special Education, Iowa Dept Education

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469739?accountid=14667

Abstract: In light of the rising need for accountability in public education, the need to demonstrate the efficacy of school social work intervention in special education is considered. It is argued that the literature provides insight into available outcomes technology (eg, pre- & postmeasurement in program evaluation); however, practitioners must commit more broadly to such procedures to elicit public & policymaker support. 9 References. Author: Reitz, Cindy1; Lindgren, Nancy1 Northern Trails Area Education Agency, Clear Lake, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61531941?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article is the second of a two-part paper on Attention-Deficit Hyperactivity Disorder (ADHD). Assessment & diagnosis were covered previously in the Dec 1989 issue. The present article addresses the stressors associated with parenting an ADHD child & the implications for effective interventions by a school social worker. Attention Deficit Hyperactivity Disorder: An Annotated Bibliography (Part II)

Author: Verrette, Sallie C11 Heartland Area Education Agency II, Newton, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61419105?accountid=14667

Abstract: This bibliography is part of a project intended to provide school social workers with easily accessible information on a variety of specialized topics. The topic of this bibliography is research on attention-deficit hyperactivity disorder published since 1980. From approximately one hundred articles, thirty-one were selected for inclusion & briefly summarized. Topics include medication, nondrug therapy, characteristics & etiology of attention-deficit hyperactivity disorder, & longitudinal & prospective studies. Part II presents articles in the categories of non-drug therapy & longitudinal & prospective studies. Part I, which appeared in the previous issue, covered the topics of characteristics & etiology & medication. 1 Reference. Adapted from the source document.

A Paradigm for Supervision of School Social Work Practicum Students

Author: Birtwistle, Dea Ellen Epley1; Lindgren, Nancy1 Northern Trails Area Education Agency, Clear Lake, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61468954?accountid=14667

Abstract: Supervision of the practicum school social worker requires a recognition of the level of intensity of supervision that is beneficial in enhancing the student's professional growth. A paradigm that emphasizes supervision as a fluid & multidimensional process & that incorporates the supervisor's & student's reactions to situations, is crucial. Knowledge of the perceptions of the practicum student enables the supervisory style to be adjusted. This article describes a paradigm for practicum supervision that emphasizes the importance of structure & process in school social work practicum supervision. Statements from a practicum student are presented parenthetically throughout the article to illustrate aspects of the paradigm. 6 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Group as the Identified Problem: A Screening Approach

Author: Pothast, Henry L11 U.S. Air Force Biomedical Sciences Corps, Sheppard Air Force Base, Wichita Fall, TX

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61465037?accountid=14667

Abstract: School social workers sometimes provide consultation services to educators who are frustrated with entire groups of pupils. Such groups are often labeled "difficult" & require systematic screening to identify target problems of individual members. A problem identification method is presented, & practice applications of the procedure are illustrated. 8 References. Adapted from the source document.

Mediating Effects of Family Type and Process upon Self-Concepts of Adolescents

Author: Nunn, Gerald D11 Area Education Agency 6, Marshalltown, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61465050?accountid=14667

Abstract: The present study examined the effect of family type (intact vs father-loss divorce) & family process (happy vs unhappy family adjustment) upon the self-concepts of adolescents. A total of 633 students in grades 5 through 10 participated. Results indicate that both family structure & process mediate the level of self-concepts of the adolescents sampled. Students from divorced-unhappy homes had significantly lower self-concepts than all other comparison groups, while students from intact-happy homes held the highest. Future research is discussed. 1 Table, 10 References. Adapted from the source document.

School social work with victims of trauma

Author: Williams, Mary Beth

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/42389279?accountid=14667

Abstract: In daily practice, school social workers encounter children who have been exposed to a variety of stressful events. Traumatic events -- that is those outside the range of normal, everyday experience -- vary in kind. They may include the death of a parent, teacher or friend; witnessing murder, violence, or parental battering; physical and/or sexual abuse; or falling victim to a natural or manmade disaster. Therefore, the school social worker needs a working knowledge of crisis intervention and of treatment for post-traumatic stress. This article presents twelve general counseling principles which may be modified to fit the age and/or developmental stage of the child who is dealing with the aftereffects of trauma. [Author Abstract]

School Social Work Involvement in Combating Child Sexual Abuse: A Continuing Need

Author: Pothast, Henry L1; Harrington, Howard1 Sheppard AFB, Wichita Falls, TX

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469035?accountid=14667

Abstract: Because of their professional background & practice setting, social workers in schools are in a position to exercise leadership in dealing with child sexual abuse. However, there is a dearth of literature concerning a response to this problem by school practitioners. There continues to be a need for school-based efforts in several areas: (a) awareness, identification, & reporting; (b) follow-up; & (c) prevention. The current status of efforts in each of these areas is outlined, & practice implications are discussed. 24 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Place of the School Experience: A Content Analysis of Recent Social Work Literature

Author: Verrette, Sallie C11 Heartland Area Education Agency, Newton, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61495005?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article summarizes a content analysis of 118 articles dealing with children's issues published in three major social work journals form 1985 through 1989. The importance of the school experience is briefly discussed together with the fact that a large majority of the articles reviewed made only brief or no reference to school or to the child in school. The significance of this finding for the school social worker is discussed. 44 References. Adapted from the source document.

A Home-Based Management Contract for Secondary Students

Author: Welch, Gary L11 Heartland Area Education Agency II

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61470687?accountid=14667

Abstract: This contractual Home-Based Management Program is the result of integrating various concepts into a consistent, simple method to improve a student's performance in both regular & special education programs in the secondary grades. The identified areas of performance include (1) passing all classes with acceptable grades; (2) completing all assignments in an acceptable manner; & (3) demonstrating appropriate behavior in the classroom when compared to other students in the same class. When the following methodology is applied, the results are encouraging for improving a student's performance in school & actively involving the student, parents, & school in a team effort. The rationale & methodology for implementation of this Home-Based Management Program are discussed in this article. 2 Appendixes, 8 References. Adapted from the source document.

Enhancing Behavior Change of Self-Contained Behavior Disordered Students through Videotaped Feedback

Author: Brown, Chuck1; Ackermann, Shelley1 Area Education Agency II, Johnston, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469050?accountid=14667

Abstract: Eight students from an urban elementary self-contained classroom participated in a videotape project designed to assist students in focusing on their own behavior & the effects of their behavior on others. The students reenacted a previously experienced conflictual situation & critiqued their own behaviors. The students were able to find positive solutions to their conflicts after reviewing the tapes. Parents who participated in a posttrial discussion believed that the use of videotaping could assist the children in seeing a variety of positive resolutions to conflict. 3 References. Adapted from the source document.

Incestuous child sexual abuse

Author: Neal, Kathryn

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/42404186?accountid=14667

Abstract: This paper reviews the relevant literature concerning incestuous child sexual abuse which has recently emerged as a signficant social problem in the United States. Social workers, particularly those in child welfare and mental health, need to develop a solid knowledge base in this content area if they are to successfully diagnose and treat this important social and personal problem. The recent Illinois Criminal Sexual Assault Act of 1984 is described and its rationale provided. Assessment procedures for child sexual abuse are described, focusing on physical, emotional, and behavioral indicators. Sgroi's seven treatment issues are discussed along with their implications for social work practice. PTSD is introduced as a new treatment issue. [Text, p. 11]

Socio-Emotional Orientation of Transfer Students: A Primary Prevention Project

Author: Pryor, Carolyn B11 School Social Work Training, Wayne State U, Detroit, MI

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469063?accountid=14667

Abstract: Students who transfer into a school are under stress in this time of transition. Previous research has concluded that they are at high risk of becoming substance abusers. Several projects directed at meeting the needs of relocating students are reviewed. A project to integrate students transferring from other secondary schools illustrates the impact of a school social worker on the entire school & community. Interviews with new students, a questionnaire, & clinical data show how the project integrated students into positive roles & provided benefits for this school. The steps involved in its implementation could apply to other system-side change efforts. 20 References. Adapted from the source document.

Group Process as a Means to Enhance Professional and Personal Growth

Author: Haynes, Meribeth1; Kimpston, Sue; McKean, Gail; Reynolds, Deborah1 Heartland Area Education Agency

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61439998?accountid=14667

Abstract: In June 1989, nine school social workers from Heartland Area Education Agency (AEA 11) participated in a five-day workshop facilitated by two of the nine members. The purpose was to learn with & from colleagues & to provide support to decrease the isolation of which many of the agency's social workers had complained in a survey the previous summer. The experience greatly exceeded all expectations. Skill enhancement was one end result, but the most significant gains for participants were the relationships formed, the professional identity strengthened, & the self-confidence restored. 2 References. Adapted from the source document.

Enhancing Professional Relationships with Families of Young Children: A Practice Challenge for School Social Workers

Author: Armstrong, Ronda Parks11 Heartland Area Education Agency 11, Johnston, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61419131?accountid=14667

Abstract: With the focus on family-centered services in early intervention for infants & toddlers due to Public Law 99-457, more attention is being drawn to the relationships among families & community professionals. School social workers can be leaders in developing or improving positive family-professional relationships. This article first reviews past parent involvement & factors affecting parent & professional perspectives. It concludes with a discussion of six major recommendations for enhancing relationships: (1) Examine current practice. (2) Decrease differences in perspectives. (3) View families as partners. (4) Strengthen team interaction. (5) Reinforce the family's decision-making role & natural support system. (6) Be an advocate. 24 References. Adapted from the source document.

Cal-Pal: A County-Wide Volunteer Service Program.

Author: Wilson, John

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/62630493?accountid=14667

Abstract: The implementation and continuing growth of a volunteer youth/adult match-up service, Cal-Pal, being provided in seven rural communities are described in this article. School social workers in these areas can collaborate with other school-based personnel and community leaders to make such a service available. A major benefit of the program is the growing number of youth who are able to enjoy the opportunity of another friendship with a responsible adult outside the family. The steps described in building this service program can be used in other communities that are interested in developing a volunteer youth and adult pal program. Essential to the effectiveness of Cal-Pal is community consensus between youth, parents, school and non-school leaders that a need exists for an individual friendship program. Beyond being aware of the need, a match-up program at the county level requires the commitment of many people who make their time and talent available to Cal-Pal service. Rural school social workers, by training and experience, are able to play a part in building interdisciplinary cooperation, assessing community needs, facilitating teamwork in group planning, and supporting the ongoing goals of the developing community service program. (RJM)

Subject: Adolescents; Children; Community Involvement; Community Services (major); Elementary Secondary Education; Friendship (major); Rural Schools (major); School Community Relationship (major); Student Needs; Student Welfare (major); Volunteers (major)

Building Inservice Programs for the Nineties and Beyond

Author: Struckman, Charlene11 Area Education Agency 7, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61472874?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article briefly describes current practices of school social workers in the development of inservice training in IA. A review of the literature on staff development describes the types of inservice training that can be offered & lists those approaches that have been defined as "best practices" in the literature. Based upon the literature review & current practice in IA, a list of five best practices for school social workers in the development of inservice programming is presented. 28 References. The Roots of School Social Work in New York City

Author: McCullagh, James G11 Dept Social Work, U Northern Iowa, Cedar Falls

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61465065?accountid=14667

Abstract: The visiting teacher movement is traced from its inception in New York City in 1905 to approximately 1913, when the New York Board of Education employed its first visiting teachers. The initial impetus came from settlement house residents who experimented with different approaches to helping the immigrant child in the home, the community, & the school. The movement, begun & led by women, & with the support of the Public Education Assoc, pioneered a new approach that had grown into an important social work field of practice. Understanding the roots of school social work may offer contemporary practitioners a sense of identity -- rootedness -- & insights as the profession faces the challenges of the 21st century. 55 References. Adapted from the source document.

School Social Work in Early Childhood Special Education: A Position Statement

Author: Clark, James P

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61440004?accountid=14667

Abstract: It is the position of the Midwest School Social Work Council that the provision of school social work services in early childhood special education programs is essential to assuring comprehensive & effective educational programming for young children & their families. 5 References. Cognitive-Behavioral Treatment of Attention Deficit Hyperactive Disorder with an Elementary School Student

Author: Kremer, Thomas11 Delaware County Mental Health Center, Manchester, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61511438?accountid=14667

Abstract: Cognitive-behavioral self-control therapy was used to decrease the amount of time that an Attention Deficit Hyperactivity Disordered & behaviorally disordered special education student spent in "time-out." Training by means of a problem-solving plan affected the subject's positive control over problematic behaviors & reduced time spent out of the classroom. Intervention was initiated after a 4-week baseline measure of the amount of time spent in time-out & continued for 6 weeks for a total of 10 weeks. The results of the multiple measure time series design were plotted on a graph & examined to determine the decrease in problematic behavior & the amount of time the subject spent in time-out. 1 Table, 2 Figures, 14 References. Adapted from the source document.

National Association of Visiting Teachers: The Early Years, 1916-1930

Author: McCullagh, James G11 Dept Social Work, U Northern Iowa, Cedar Falls

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61495038?accountid=14667

Abstract: The creation & development of the first national association for school social workers -- the National Assoc of Visiting Teachers & Home & School Visitors -- is traced from its conception to 1930. The Assoc united visiting teachers, home & school visitors, & school counselors & created a national professional identity that reflected its association with the professions of education & social work. The Assoc's leadership -- all women -- established a committee structure, sponsored annual & regional conferences, published a bulletin, newsletters, & various reports, & established qualifications for its membership, which ultimately contributed to the development of one national association for social workers. 1 Appendix, 80 References. Adapted from the source document.

Cal-Pal Update

Author: Wilson, John11 Area Education Agency 5, Rockwell City, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61495069?accountid=14667

Abstract: Wilson describes Cal-Pal, a community service program organized for the children of single-parent families in IA. This update reviews the structure & services provided in the beginning of the organization, the hopes for the future of Cal-Pal, & the current status of the program. Wilson describes Calhoun County, the service's location, as having a lower than average per capita income & few family counseling services for a relatively high number of single-parent families. Cal-Pal is designed to match responsible adults with youth from these single-parent families. Wilson then illustrates some of the aspects of the program that are distinct from other match-up services & details the beginning of the program. Various limitations of the program include nonparticipation of some communities in the county, limited number of adults, shorter than desired match-ups, & retirement of adults from the program. Wilson concludes that the current status is good & vital with the following evidence in mind: there are 55 official match-ups to date & the board has remained stable. Ahead of Cal-Pal is the development of training procedures & workshops for both prospective & current adult volunteers. 13 References. J. Backman

Stress Debriefings for School Professionals Involved in Traumatic Event Response

Author: Heer, Steve11 Keystone Area Education Agency

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61507096?accountid=14667

Abstract: Traumatic event response plans have been adopted by many schools for the purpose of meeting the needs of students after a suicide or other sudden death of a peer. They have also been useful following assaults, natural disasters, or other events that provoke significant stress responses in the school setting. What we have known all along, but only recently begun to address, is the stress response in team members themselves who offer this "psychological first aid" to students, parents, & colleagues. Stress debriefings have been offered to emergency service providers in the medical, law enforcement, & firefighting fields for several years by critical incident stress debriefings teams that comprise mental health professionals & trained peer debriefers. Those who offer analogous "psychological emergency" services in the schools could benefit from debriefings as well. This article describes debriefings & makes a case for their provision to the adults in the school setting. 4 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+School+Social+Work&amp;rft.atitle=Stress+Debriefings+for+School+Professionals+Involved+in+Traumatic+Event+Response&amp;rft.au=Heer%2C+Steve&amp;rft.aulast=Heer&amp;rft.aufirst=Steve&amp;rft.date=1995-04-01&amp;rft.volume=8&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=5&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Journal+of+School+Social+Work&amp;rft.issn=&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

The Intervention Model of School Social Work as Used by Green Valley Area Education Agency 14

Author: Harrington, Danette1; Madsen, Sally; Hanna, Kaye; Hight, Lora; Franklin, Ray; Sickels, Sandra1 Green Valley Area Education Agency 14

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469541?accountid=14667

Abstract: The Green Valley Area Education Agency 14 social workers have evolved a model of school social work practice that delivers direct intervention services. This intervention model focuses on direct, action-oriented interventions. Individual, family, & group counseling are the most common services offered. Consultation with parents, administrators, teachers & staff, the use of a Crisis Intervention Team, & linkage & referrals to community services are other important features of the Intervention Model. 5 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Formation of the School Social Work Association of America

Author: Struckman, Charlene11 Area Education Agency 7

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61511487?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article provides a brief history of the events that preceded the school social work leadership retreat that was held in IL in July 1994. Several participants' experiences show the similarities & differences in school social work practice that exist from state to state. Such shared experiences affirm the value of school social workers learning from one another in a national forum. Reasons behind the growing consensus to establish a separate national school social work association will be described. 7 References. Adapted from the source document.

Improving Services for Students with Behavior Disorders

Author: Struckman, Charlene1; Darrah, Frank; Sinclair, Dennis1 Area Education Agency 7

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469073?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article describes a study that is based on a literature review; a review of student files; & a written survey of teachers, principals, & support special education staff. The purpose of the study was to gain insight that would help to reduce the number of students with behavior disorders who require special education services & to enable more of these students to be successful in the regular education mainstream. The results of the study indicate a need for more training for regular education teachers regarding behavior interventions, managing children with Attention Deficit Hyperactivity Disorder, & problem solving. The study also indicates a need for better communication between regular & special education teachers & clearer exit criteria for students to leave special education. 1 Appendix, 25 References. Adapted from the source document.

Jane Day -- First Visiting Teacher: "You Did a Noble Work and Did it Well"

Author: McCullagh, James G11 Dept Social Work, U Northern Iowa, Cedar Falls

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469554?accountid=14667

Abstract: Jane Day, from New Albany, IN, & a teacher for many years, became the first full-time visiting teacher & the first social worker to work from within the public schools soon after becoming the first school social worker to obtain social work training. She, in 1908 on Manhattan's Lower East Side, became the official, school-based link between the home & school & community for the child's welfare. By her professionalism & character, she demonstrated the invaluable & unique contributions made by visiting teachers & spurred the hiring of additional visiting teachers in New York City. 34 References. Adapted from the source document.

Causes of Burnout among School Social Workers and Possible Preventive Measures

Author: Greene, Jilleen1; Raschick, Michael1 Albany School District, MN

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61469100?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article explores the phenomenon of burnout in school social workers working in a midwestern city. It specifically looks at what may contribute to burnout & ways that it can be prevented. The article is based on research that used the Maslach Burnout inventory to measure the degree workers were experiencing depersonalization, emotional exhaustion, & loss of a sense of personal accomplishment. The study looked at possible relationships between various worker variables & their Maslach scores. These variables included worker demographic data as well as measures of their job satisfaction, work duties, & the type & amount of social support they received both on & off the job. Study participants were asked their opinion about the causes of burnout & ways to prevent it. Results indicated that feelings of emotional exhaustion are related to a lack of supervisory support, while a sense of personal accomplishment is a function of overall job satisfaction. 4 Tables, 16 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+School+Social+Work&amp;rft.atitle=Causes+of+Burnout+among+School+Social+Workers+and+Possible+Preventive+Measures&amp;rft.au=Greene%2C+Jilleen%3BRaschick%2C+Michael&amp;rft.aulast=Greene&amp;rft.aufirst=Jilleen&amp;rft.date=1998-05-01&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.issue=1-2&amp;rft.spage=4&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Journal+of+School+Social+Work&amp;rft.issn=&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Solution Building in the Schools

Author: Walsh, Elizabeth11 Dept Psychiatry, UIHC

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61468972?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article describes the application of the solution-focused model of intervention, which was developed by Steve deShazer & Insoo Kim Berg, to working with children, families, & professional teams in the schools. Reflections of an Iowa Freshman Legislator

Author: Foege, Ro11 State Representative, 50th House District, Mount Vernon, IA rfoege@legis.state.ia.us

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61532052?accountid=14667

Abstract: Ro Foege, school social worker, was elected to the Iowa State Legislature in the fall of 1996. He was asked by the IJSSW to write about his first-year experience as a state legislator. The article that follows is a personal & political statement about his experience & his viewpoints. It is an inside "look" into the legislative process & offers readers insight into the workings of state government & decision-making issues. It is full of concern about issues that are of paramount importance for school social workers & social workers in general. We assume that other areas of the country have somewhat similar issues & concerns. Adapted from the source document.

Looking over My Shoulder

Author: Huxtable, Marion11 Tucson Unified School District, AZ

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61466027?accountid=14667

Abstract: It is not often that we have the chance to learn the frustrations & satisfactions of a colleague. Readers may catch their own reflection as they look over the shoulder of a school social worker, whose life work has been down at eye level with children. I have found satisfaction in balancing my work helping children succeed in school with strengthening our profession with colleagues around the country & starting to build a global network of school social workers. 11 References. Adapted from the source document.

Educational Placement for Children with Behavioral and/or Emotional Disorders: Overlooked Variables Contributing to Placements in Restrictive Settings

Author: Frey, Andy11 Kent School Social Work, U Louisville, KY ajfrey@gwise.louisville.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61465473?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article discusses often-overlooked variables contributing to educational placement decisions for children with behavioral &/or emotional disorders in the public schools. A brief outline of the educational placement controversy is first provided to readers, followed by the relevance of educational placement decisions to school social work. The remainder of the paper considers the extent that personal bias influences placement decisions for historically oppressed populations. Specifically, the contribution of gender, socioeconomic status (SES), & ethnicity are entertained. The implications concerning school social work practice, social work education, education policy, & research are also discussed. 40 References. Adapted from the source document.

Joining the "In Crowd": The Social Interactions and Peer Relations of Preadolescent Youth

Author: Hepler, Juanita B11 School Social Work, Boise State U, ID

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61438747?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article discusses the critical role of social development for children as well as the factors that impact on a child's acceptance by peers. The problems that children encounter in their social interactions, even in integrated settings, & the impact of gender issues & gender stereotypes on social interactions are reviewed. The author also discusses the results of observational data collected on the social interactions of 6 5th-grade girls with learning disabilities. Suggestions for addressing issues related to social development & acceptance in the school setting are included. 2 Tables, 34 References. Adapted from the source document.

Becoming a School Social Worker: The Concept of Equi-Finality

Author: Levine, Renee Shai

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61463614?accountid=14667

Abstract: The concept of equifinality is used to frame the process by which the author became a school social worker. It describes the varied paths she took to balance the responsibilities of a wife & mother, while maintaining her professional activities. It is heartening to note that, despite limited work hours & waiting to move into the academic setting until after her children were into their own school experiences, she was able to do research, publish, teach, become active in professional organizations, move into a school social work setting, & in other ways make a contribution to the field. She recently retired from the practice of school social work & continues to remain active. 27 References. Adapted from the source document.

Intervention to Prevention: An Evolutionary Process

Author: Davis, I Lorraine

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61467301?accountid=14667

Abstract: Most people's lives follow an evolutionary process, whether or not they recognize it as it is occurring. I would wager that we do not, per se, consciously know all the turns in the road & where they are leading. We set our goals, & these may change as we experiment with our inherent talents. At some fork in the road, there is a "knowing" that it is time for evaluation of our situation. Either we forge ahead on the course we are following, or we make adjustments. Listening clearly to that inner voice, following our instincts, & engaging in some thoughtful planning, we may just reach the galaxy for which we are aiming. The author's personal development as a school social worker is chronicled, highlighting her activities with female delinquents at the Wisconsin School for Girls. 10 References. Adapted from the source document.

Reflections on Twenty-Five Years as a School Social Worker: Joys and Lessons from the Long Haul

Author: Armstrong, Ronda Parks11 Heartland Area Education Agency, Johnston, IA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61467929?accountid=14667

Abstract: Each person brings a unique story & approach to the school social work role. This narrative highlights what I have learned in my 25 years as a school social worker with a varied career: pioneer, author, state consultant, professional organization leader, practicum student instructor, mentor, interagency collaborator, & local district team member. Joys & lessons are organized among four main themes -- relationships, responsibility, resilience, & resourcefulness -- interwoven with the perspective of my personal journey with special needs, life-threatening medical conditions, resilience, & empowerment. 15 References. Sexual Minority Students and Peer Sexual Harassment in High School

Author: Fineran, Susan11 School Social Work, Boston U, MA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60445877?accountid=14667

Abstract: Explores relationships among sexual orientation, gender, peer relationships, & peer sexual harassment victimization for 712 suburban high school students, ages 14-19, in MA. Sexual minority students experienced sexual harassment more frequently than heterosexual students, & sexual minority students & heterosexual girls reported being significantly more upset & threatened by peer sexual harassment victimization. In addition, sexual minority students identified unfamiliar male schoolmates as primary perpetrators & were physically assaulted more frequently than heterosexual students. 4 Tables, 1 Figure, 25 References. Adapted from the source document.

A Macro Approach to Meet the Challenge of No Child Left Behind

Author: Thiede, Charlene E11 Bureau Children/Family/Community Services, Iowa Dept Education Des Moines

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61346269?accountid=14667

Abstract: The No Child Left Behind (NCLB) Act increased the pressure for public schools to improve the academic achievement of groups of students that are poor, disabled, or from minority backgrounds. The author presents a macropractice model that school social workers can use to help schools implement systemic strategies to improve the academic achievement of students. The model is illustrated with a case example: a series of family reading workshops collaboratively planned & implemented by a school social worker in a racially diverse elementary school. The author describes the macropractice change episode, reviews the pre- & post-intervention test data & makes suggestions for possible future research. 4 Figures, 51 References. Adapted from the source document.

Beyond Problem Solving: The Social Worker as Risk Manager and Educator in Educatonal-Host Settings

Author: Kelly, Diann Cameron11 School Social Work, Adelphi U, Garden City, NY

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61366101?accountid=14667

Abstract: Whether the educational-host settings are schools, after-school centers, early child development programs, or community youth centers, these educational-host settings can pose significant hazards to ethical social work practice. This article discusses the need for social workers to engage in risk management & ethics education to address ethical dilemmas. By implementing these critical roles in school social work practice, the school social worker may be less isolated & better prepared to develop an ethically based, transformational practice. 1 Figure, 24 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Debate Surrounding Psychotropic Medication Usage in Young Children

Author: Waller, Raymond J1; Lewellen, Kathy; Bresson, Diane1 Piedmont Coll Athens, GA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61366737?accountid=14667

Abstract: There is current debate & concern surrounding the practice of prescribing psychoactive medications in children, especially children in their preschool & elementary school years. Although the practice of prescribing these medications is on the rise, research supporting this practice is insufficient. This article raises concerns about medication use in young children. Although school social workers do not prescribe medication & cannot give medical advice, it is critical for school social workers to understand the decisions & issues facing families of children who may be considered for treatment with psychotropic medications. 25 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=The+Debate+Surrounding+Psychotropic+Medication+Usage+in+Young+Children&amp;rft.au=Waller%2C+Raymond+J%3BLewellen%2C+Kathy%3BBresson%2C+Diane&amp;rft.aulast=Waller&amp;rft.aufirst=Raymond&amp;rft.date=2005-04-01&amp;rft.volume=29&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.spage=53&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.issn=01615653&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

The Use of Stimulent Medication for Treatment of Attention-Deficit/Hyperactivity Disorder: A Survey of School Social Workers' Knowledge, Opinions/Attitudes, and Experience

Author: Cornell-Swanson, La Vonne1; Irwin, Melissa; Johnson, Kim; Bowman, Krista; Frankenberger, William1 Human Development Center, U Wisconsin, Eau Claire

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61371110?accountid=14667

Abstract: This study examined school social workers' knowledge, opinions/attitudes, & experience regarding Attention-Deficit/Hyperactivity Disorder (ADHD), including treatment with stimulant medication. Participants consisted of 189 school social workers from throughout the United States. The surveyed school social workers appear to be uninformed about controversial issues related to children diagnosed with ADHD that are being treated with stimulant medication. The participants seemed to have dissonant views about whether ADHD symptoms may be caused by either neurobiological &/or environmental factors. Regarding treatment, school social workers surveyed believed that behavioral programs could be effective interventions for children diagnosed with ADHD. However, they report that they are generally uninvolved in any form of follow-up after children are placed on medication. The school social workers reported that nearly 25% of their caseloads were students with ADHD, & that classroom teachers made 58.7% of the initial referrals for ADHD. Implications of the study are discussed. 3 Tables, 38 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=The+Use+of+Stimulent+Medication+for+Treatment+of+Attention-Deficit%2FHyperactivity+Disorder%3A+A+Survey+of+School+Social+Workers%27+Knowledge%2C+Opinions%2FAttitudes%2C+and+Experience&amp;rft.au=Cornell-Swanson%2C+La+Vonne%3BIrwin%2C+Melissa%3BJohnson%2C+Kim%3BBowman%2C+Krista%3BFrankenberger%2C+William&amp;rft.aulast=Cornell-Swanson&amp;rft.aufirst=La&amp;rft.date=2005-04-01&amp;rft.volume=29&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.spage=62&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.issn=01615653&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

A Comparative Analysis of Substances Used by Suicidal and Non-Suicidal High School Students

Author: Manetta, Ameda A1; Ormand, Teresa1 Winthrop U, Rockhill, SC

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61346313?accountid=14667

Abstract: The majority of studies on suicidal behaviors are based on populations already diagnosed with clinical disorders. These studies have acknowledged that substance use is related to suicidal behaviors, yet the relationship of specific substances has not been identified. In this study a sub-sample of 4,828 suicidal & non-suicidal adolescents who completed the 2001 Youth Risk Behavior Survey was used. A logistic regression model identified that alcohol & inhalants showed the two strongest associations to suicidal behaviors. In our discussion we identify various screening tools available that school social workers could use to implement prevention strategies in schools. 3 Tables, 32 References. Adapted from the source document.

America Is from Mars, Europe Is from Venus: How the United States Can Learn from Europe's Social Work Response to School Shootings

Author: Klein, Jessie11 Dept Sociology & Social Work, City U New York, Bronx jklein9797@aol.com

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61392613?accountid=14667

Abstract: American responses to recent school shootings have focused on security & punishment, but European nations have called for hiring more school social workers & improving student-teacher relationships. Using George Lakoff's strict father versus nurturant mother/parent model, this paper argues that the conservative, punishment-& security-based U.S approach stems from values associated with masculinity, whereas the social-value European responses are "feminine" approaches. Causes & policy responses are charted in a media analysis of recent U.S. & European shootings, showing striking patterns. Distinct causes across the Atlantic speak to different societal standards & expectations for students. Recommendations are made for new school social work initiatives in U.S. schools based on European models. 2 Tables, 90 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=America+Is+from+Mars%2C+Europe+Is+from+Venus%3A+How+the+United+States+Can+Learn+from+Europe%27s+Social+Work+Response+to+School+Shootings&amp;rft.au=Klein%2C+Jessie&amp;rft.aulast=Klein&amp;rft.aufirst=Jessie&amp;rft.date=2005-10-01&amp;rft.volume=30&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=1&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.issn=01615653&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Using a Needs Assessment to Develop Plans for Macro-Level Parent Involvement in Schools

Author: Randolph, Karen A1; Ackerman, Georgia1 School Social Work, Florida State U, Tallahassee

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61366754?accountid=14667

Abstract: Public Law 107-110, the No Child Left Behind Act of 2001 (NCLB), is the most recent in a number of policy initiatives to improve the nation's educational system. A major focus of this legislation is to increase parent involvement in schools, with an emphasis on expanding their roles in macro-level oversight & governance. In preparation for involving parents in safety planning at one suburban elementary school, we conducted a needs assessment to determine similarities & differences between family members & school staff with regard to their perceptions of school & neighborhood factors affecting child safety. This paper describes the results of the needs assessment & how we used these results to develop strategies for engaging parents in the development of a school safety plan. 2 Tables, 29 References. Adapted from the source document.

Stop and Think: An Impulse Control Program in a School Setting

Author: Caselman, Tonia D11 Dept Social Work, U Oklahoma, Tulsa tcaselman@ou.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61378826?accountid=14667

Abstract: The problems associated with impulsivity are easily recognized as some of the most serious challenges facing schools today. Impulsivity is not only a barrier for learning; it has been associated with poor social & emotional adjustment & with school violence. This paper discusses the concept of impulsivity & research. An intervention model for kindergarten through fourth-grade school social workers is presented based on empirical findings of effective interventions. Issues of assessment are addressed & specific techniques are described. 62 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=Stop+and+Think%3A+An+Impulse+Control+Program+in+a+School+Setting&amp;rft.au=Caselman%2C+Tonia+D&amp;rft.aulast=Caselman&amp;rft.aufirst=Tonia&amp;rft.date=2005-10-01&amp;rft.volume=30&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=40&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.issn=01615653&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Legal Aspects of Hyperactivity Medication in the Schools: What School Social Workers Need to Know

Author: Mason, Susan E1; Pollack, Daniel1 Wurzweiler School Social Work, Yeshiva U, NY masonse@yu.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61378891?accountid=14667

Abstract: School social workers often work with children who have been diagnosed with Attention Deficit Hyperactivity Disorder (ADHD). While laws pertaining to treating this disorder vary from state to state, there are basic legal principles & case law that apply to school social work practice. This article outlines key legal issues that school social workers may encounter when working with children & families & provides practice suggestions. 35 References. Adapted from the source document.

Educational Placement of Children with Cochlear Implants

Author: Waller, Raymond J1; Conley, Michael1 Piedmont Coll, Athens Center, GA rjwaller@yahoo.com

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61384570?accountid=14667

Abstract: Children with cochlear implants who graduated from the Auditory-Verbal Center of Atlanta, GA, were surveyed. The survey determined the educational placement of these graduates. The results indicate most of the graduates were integrated into the regular education setting. Early intervention that leads to language development appears to reduce the impact of hearing impairment on student placement into mainstream academic settings. School social workers, functioning as interdisciplinary team members for students with disabilities, have a unique opportunity to provide education, advocacy, & placement input for children with hearing impairments into the most appropriate, least restrictive educational environment. 1 Table, 12 References. Adapted from the source document.

Out of the Darkness: Male Adolescents and the Experience of Sexual Victimization

Author: Bogin, Gina Yellin11 Waubonsie Valley High School, Aurora, IL gina_bogin@ipsd.org

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61374463?accountid=14667

Abstract: Although various research studies all report considerable numbers of men who have been victims of sexual aggression, there seems to be a lack of awareness of male victims in our schools. Due to this lack of awareness, male victimization is often not considered when assessing a male student's behavior. Boys are routinely referred for disciplinary action rather than to supportive services for assessment. This article discusses male adolescents & the experience of sexual victimization. It discusses Rape Trauma Syndrome, academic issues, school-safety issues, & sexual-identity issues that may be experienced after victimization. Different treatment methods are suggested. Furthermore, therapeutic issues that are unique to the male experience are contemplated. Finally, the school social worker's role in both prevention & assisting these students is considered. References. Adapted from the source document.

A Pilot Study Examining the Social Validity and Effectiveness of a Positive Behavior Support Model in Head Start

Author: Frey, Andy1; Faith, Tera; Ellitt, Anissa; Royer, Brooke1 Kent School Social Work, U Louisville, KY afrey@louisville.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61374828?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article examines the social validity & effectiveness of the universal intervention component (classroom management) of a positive behavior support (PBS) model in Head Start classrooms. Universal interventions were implemented in seven Head Start classrooms by graduate-level social work students serving as mental health consultants. Social validity was systematically assessed via satisfaction surveys & focus-group interviews of Head Start staff Effectiveness was evaluated by comparing the environments of seven classrooms that received the intervention with seven comparison classrooms that did not receive the intervention. The satisfaction surveys & focus-group interviews yielded positive results, which stressed the importance of collaboration, buy-in, skills of consultants, quality of relationship building, amount of input into the plan, & behavioral/academic outcomes. Effectiveness results revealed some minor differences in the classroom environment between the experimental & comparison-group classrooms, but these were not significant. Findings indicated that key stakeholders perceived the universal intervention as having worthy goals & objectives & that they had high levels of satisfaction with the implementation effort. The limitations of the current study & implications for school social workers are discussed. Tables, Appendixes, References. Adapted from the source document.

Cash through Collaboration: A Relational Approach to Grant Writing for Social Workers in Schools

Author: Raines, James C1; Alvarez, Michelle1 School Social Work, Illinois State U, Normal

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61374457?accountid=14667

Abstract: Grant writing is an increasingly important skill as schools face funding shortages. This article will teach the basic components of grant writing. Four basic principles of grant writing that every novice should know are building relationships with investors, using a team approach, capitalizing on capabilities, & tackling the project one piece at a time. It is essential that beginning grant writers prepare a concept paper understand the different types of grants, learn how to locate the right funder & stay current with national trends. Components of a proposal include the title page, abstract, problem statement, program description, staffing, budget, & evaluation plan. Funders are divided into three categories: corporations, foundations, & government. New grant seekers are encouraged to start locally before moving up to state & national sources. Getting funded depends on meeting the funder's criteria, understanding that denials are only temporary, & knowing that acceptances are just the beginning of a relationship with the funder. Appendixes, References. Adapted from the source document.

Examining the Association between Academic Achievement and Self-Esteem in African American Male Youth in a Community-Outreach After-School Program

Author: Teasley, Martell L1; Lee, Earle1 Coll Social Work, Florida State U, Tallahassee mteasley@mailer.fsu.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61391721?accountid=14667

Abstract: The purpose of this study is to investigate the impact of a community-outreach after-school academic enhancement program on self-reported levels of self-esteem in African American male youth ages eight to eighteen (N = 5 1). Using survey research methods, two research questions are asked: (1) Will youth with higher levels of academic achievement report higher levels of self-esteem than youth with lower levels of academic achievement? And (2) Are levels of program satisfaction related to levels of academic achievement &, therefore, levels of self-esteem in participants; The analyses revealed that higher GPAs are related to higher levels of school self-esteem in participants & that school self-esteem is related to member program satisfaction scores. Findings from this study may provide new research information about levels of self-esteem in African American male youth with similar ethnic & social experiences as well as promote evidence-based practice for social work professionals engaging in community outreach programs. Tables, References. Adapted from the source document.

Special Education Advocacy: An Intervention Program

Author: Green, Denise M1; Twill, Sarah1 School Social Work, U Georgia, Athens dmgreen@uga.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61378868?accountid=14667

Abstract: The Special Education Advocacy (SEA) program was initiated in 2001 to address the growing concerns of the overrepresentation of special-education students involved with the juvenile court in a large, southern metropolitan city. The SEA has recently completed its fourth year of service in this city. This study evaluated the first two years of service. The Special Education Advocacy Coordinator (SFAQ) determines if the school is fulfilling its obligation to provide a free & appropriate education to special-education students processed by the juvenile court system. The SEAC's services range from administrative file reviews to case management to helping find appropriate school placements. This atheoretical, formative, & exploratory program evaluation collected data concerning demographic makeup, state-defined recidivism, overall recidivism, & SEAC-provided services. The program is innovative, serving an overrepresented population within juvenile court systems, & certainly is worthy of review by other court systems grappling with this population of youth. Tables, References. Adapted from the source document.

History of School Social Work: The Illinois Perspective

Author: Morrison, Vaughn

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61379985?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article provides the reader with an overview of important historical moments in the school social work profession from the perspective & contributions of school social workers in Illinois. Illinois was chosen for two reasons: (1) nationally, Illinois has universally been considered the leader in the school social work field almost from the beginning of the profession & (2) the author, from Illinois, was an active participant in many of the examples provided. Breaking from standard journal-article format, readers are invited to test their knowledge of school social work history in the United States by taking a quiz. Adapted from the source document.

One Hundred Years of Linking Schools with Communities: Current Models and Opportunities

Author: Franklin, Cynthia1; Gerlach, Beth1 School Social Work, U Texas Austin

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61397422?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article reviews the evolution of school-community partnerships by examining the past, present, & future trends in school-based practice. Additionally, it discusses the adaptations that school social workers have made in the past to meet changing demands in school environments. Suggestions are made for the skills needed to advance school-community partnerships in the present day context of school social work practice, Finally, the article reviews the invaluable role that school social workers offer in the advancement of school-community-linked services. School social workers are encouraged to continue to provide leadership in the creation of school-community partnerships that focus on improving academic achievement. References. Adapted from the source document.

The Complexity of Confidentiality in Schools Today: The School Social Worker Context

Author: Kopels, Sandra1; Lindsey, Brenda Coble1 School Social Work, U Illinois Urbana-Champaign kopels@uiuc.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61359916?accountid=14667

Abstract: The role of the school social worker has changed significantly since its beginning as the liaison between schools & immigrant children in settlement houses. Today, school social work roles have significantly expanded to keep pace with the problems commonly found in schools. The literature written for the field of school social work reflects the complexity of social problems that school social workers face in their professional practice. A quandary for school social workers is how to balance competing demands for information about students while trying to respect their privacy & maintain confidentiality. This article reviews the NASW Code of Ethics, position statements of professional school social work organizations, & scholarly literature to provide guidance for school social workers in maintaining student confidentiality. Because scant attention has been paid to legal issues & their impact on confidentiality, this article discusses factors such as the duty to warn, the imminence of harm, the age of the child, & who the school social worker's client is. References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=The+Complexity+of+Confidentiality+in+Schools+Today%3A+The+School+Social+Worker+Context&amp;rft.au=Kopels%2C+Sandra%3BLindsey%2C+Brenda+Coble&amp;rft.aulast=Kopels&amp;rft.aufirst=Sandra&amp;rft.date=2006-07-01&amp;rft.volume=30&amp;rft.issue=special+issue&amp;rft.spage=63&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.issn=01615653&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

(One Hundred and) Ten Years Later. Students in Foster Care Still Need Our Help!

Author: Altshuler, Sandra J11 School Social Work, Eastern Washington U, Cheney saltshuler@mail.ewu.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61397484?accountid=14667

Abstract: Although the first one hundred years of school social work included support for the needs of the most vulnerable & disenfranchised students attending public schools, until recently little attention has been given to the needs of children in foster care, who may be the most vulnerable children in the public schools. This article presents a brief historical review of the educational struggles of children in foster care, the developing knowledge base about the psycho-educational needs of students who live in foster care, & best school social worker practice in the twenty-first century to support the needs of these highly vulnerable students. Current research suggests that there is a need for increased collaborative efforts with both the child welfare system & foster parents & for persistent advocacy within the school environment to support both a welcoming & educationally appropriate environment to meet the unique needs of each student. References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=%28One+Hundred+and%29+Ten+Years+Later.+Students+in+Foster+Care+Still+Need+Our+Help%21&amp;rft.au=Altshuler%2C+Sandra+J&amp;rft.aulast=Altshuler&amp;rft.aufirst=Sandra&amp;rft.date=2006-07-01&amp;rft.volume=30&amp;rft.issue=special+issue&amp;rft.spage=79&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=School+Social+Work+Journal&amp;rft.issn=01615653&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

School Social Work in the Twenty-First Century: Current Trends and Challenges in Best Practice with Mental Health Issues

Author: Massat, Carol Rippey1; Ornstein, Eric; Moses, Helene1 Jane Addams Coll Social Work, U Illinois, Chicago cmassat@uic.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61382190?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article describes trends & challenges that affect school social work best practice with mental health concerns that are commonly presented in schools. The authors describe evolving needs of students, evolving models of service, & a new emphasis on stigma reduction. The article also discusses the increased emphasis on measurement, the use of the Diagnostic & Statistical Manual (DSM-IV-TR) in schools, & the evidence base for mental health interventions. Specific disorders addressed are attention deficit hyperactivity disorder, conduct disorders, mood disorders, & anxiety disorders. Tables, References. Adapted from the source document.
